GT Equivalence Verification (PO9)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is
\[
0.3064552763\sin t\;-\;0.4243105872\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.9272891093\,x\big(0.06821634757|v|^{1/3}+1\big)\;-\;1.9272891093\,x.
\]
Key structural requirements:

1) **Time term**: exactly a single sinusoid in \(t\) with constant amplitude, no \(x\) or \(v\) factor. A candidate can use \(\cos(t+\phi)\) since \(\cos(t+\phi)=\sin(t+\phi+\pi/2)\); so cosine-with-phase is fine.

2) **Damping polynomial term**: \(-0.4243\,v(1-x^2)=(-0.4243)v + (0.4243) v x^2\). So candidates must be able to produce **both** a \(v\) term and a \(v x^2\) term with opposite signs (achievable via free coefficients).

3) **Nonlinear friction/stiffness term**: \(-1.9273\,x(0.0682|v|^{1/3}+1)\) contains **\(x|v|^{1/3}\)** (absolute value and fractional power) plus an \(x\) term.

4) **Extra linear stiffness**: another \(-1.9273 x\). Net linear-in-\(x\) coefficient in GT is \(-1.9273(1+1)=-3.8545782186\) multiplying \(x\), in addition to the \(-1.9273\cdot 0.0682\,x|v|^{1/3}\) part.

So any matching candidate must be able to represent an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term (or an exactly equivalent form). **Any candidate that only has \(v^{c}\) without Abs cannot match globally** because \(v^{1/3}\) (real cube root) equals \(\operatorname{sgn}(v)|v|^{1/3}\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\); and for non-integer fractional exponents it may not even be real for negative \(v\). The problem statement is strict about negative \(v\), so Abs matters.

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–10 (polynomial/power in \(v\), no \(|v|^{1/3}\))
All have combinations of \(v\), \(v x^2\), cosine-in-\(t\), and terms like \(v^{c}x\) or \(x(c+v)^p\), plus extra \(x\) powers.
- They **can** match the \(v\) and \(vx^2\) pieces by setting coefficients.
- They **can** match the sinusoid via \(c2\cos(c3+t)\) with phase shift to become \(0.3064\sin t\).
- But they **cannot** produce \(x|v|^{1/3}\) because they have no Abs and no log/tanh mechanism that could equal \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\).  
Therefore **1–10 cannot match**.

(10 has \(x\cdot \text{Abs}(x)\), but GT needs \(\text{Abs}(v)\), not \(\text{Abs}(x)\).)

### Candidates 11–16 (log(Abs(v)+1) and/or tanh, plus polynomial terms)
These introduce \(x\log(c\,|v|+1)\) (good: has Abs(v)), but GT needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\), not a log.
- Could \(\log(a|v|+1)\) equal \(b|v|^{1/3}\) for all \(v\)? No: different functional forms (logarithmic vs power). They can coincide at isolated points, not identically.
- Extra terms like \(tanh(c x)\), \(x^4\), etc. can be zeroed by setting coefficients to 0, but the core mismatch remains.
Thus **11–16 cannot match**.

### Candidates 17–18 (cos + polynomial + x*log(Abs(v)+1))
Same issue: \(x\log(\cdot)\) cannot equal \(x|v|^{1/3}\) identically. **No match**.

### Candidates 19–30 (tanh + x*log(Abs(v)+1) + various extra terms)
Again, only non-polynomial dependence on \(v\) is via \(\log(c|v|+1)\) (or sometimes tanh in \(x\)), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). No identity can convert log to a pure power for all real \(v\). **19–30 cannot match**.

### Candidates 31–34 (extra trig factors or shifted powers, still no Abs(v) power)
- 31 adds \(x\cos(c8+c9 t)\): GT has no \(x\)-modulated time sinusoid, so must set that coefficient to 0; then it reduces to the earlier non-Abs power family.
- 32 has \(x(c7+v)^{c8}\): no Abs(v).
- 33 has \(v\cos(\cdot)\): GT has no \(v\)-modulated time sinusoid; must set to 0.
- 34 has \(v(c8+x)^4\): wrong structure.
All still cannot produce \(x|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### Candidates 35–41 (tanh and \(v^{c}x\), sometimes \(v|v|\))
These have terms like \(v^{c7}x\) or \(v\text{Abs}(v)\).
- \(v\text{Abs}(v)=\operatorname{sgn}(v)\,v^2\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\).
- \(v^{p}x\) without Abs cannot equal \(x|v|^{1/3}\) globally on negative \(v\) under the strict domain rule.
So **35–41 cannot match**.

### Candidates 42 and 44 (contain \(v\text{Abs}(v)\) and \(x(c+v)^p\))
Same mismatch: \(v\text{Abs}(v)\) is quadratic-like with sign, not \(|v|^{1/3}\). Also \(x(c+v)^p\) cannot become \(x|v|^{1/3}\) for all real \(v\). **No match**.

### Candidate 43 (log(c6*v+1) without Abs)
Even worse: \(\log(c6 v+1)\) not defined for all negative \(v\) unless restricted domain, which is not allowed here; and not a power anyway. **No match**.

### Candidate 45, 48 (tanh + polynomial + \(v^{c}x\), no Abs(v) power)
No way to get \(x|v|^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 46 (has \(x\text{Abs}(x)\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\))
Wrong absolute value variable and wrong dependence. **No match**.

### Candidate 47 (has \(x^{c4}\) and \(v^{c8}x\), no Abs(v))
Cannot match \(x|v|^{1/3}\) globally. **No match**.

### Candidate 49 (has \(x^{c5}\) and \(v^{c7}x\), no Abs(v))
Same. **No match**.

### Candidate 50 (tanh + polynomial + \(v^{c}x\), no Abs(v) power)
Same. **No match**.

**Conclusion:** None of the candidates contain a term capable of representing the GT’s essential \(x\,|v|^{1/3}\) dependence (with Abs on \(v\) and fractional power) in a globally valid way over negative and positive \(v\). Everything else (sinusoid in \(t\), \(v\) and \(vx^2\), linear \(x\)) could be tuned, but this missing functional form prevents exact equivalence.

**GT:** `-0.424310587218182*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.92728910930903*x*(0.0682163475684738*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.92728910930903*x + 0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.424310587218182*v + 0.424310587218182*v*x**2`
- `-1.92728910930903*0.0682163475684738*x*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 1.92728910930903*x`

Combining:
- `v` term: `-0.424310587218182*v`
- `v*x²` term: `+0.424310587218182*v*x**2`
- `x*|v|^(1/3)` term: `-0.131520519...x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
- `x` term: `-1.92728910930903*x - 1.92728910930903*x = -3.85457821861806*x`
- `sin(t)` term: `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

**GT structure:** `A*v + B*v*x² + C*x*|v|^(1/3) + D*x + E*sin(t)`

The key basis functions are: `v`, `v*x²`, `x*|v|^(1/3)`, `x`, `sin(t)`.

Now let me check each candidate. The critical question for most candidates is whether they can produce the term `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates 1-10, 31-50:** These contain terms like `v**c5*x` and/or `v**c8*x`. The term `v**c*x` with `c=1/3` gives `v^(1/3)*x`, NOT `|v|^(1/3)*x`. Since `v` takes both positive and negative values, `v^(1/3)` is NOT the same as `|v|^(1/3)`. For odd fractional powers, `v^(1/3)` is an odd function while `|v|^(1/3)` is an even function. So these cannot match unless they have TWO such terms that combine to give `|v|^(1/3)`.

For candidates with two `v**c*x` terms (like Candidates 4, 5, etc.): Setting `c5=1/3` and `c8=1/3` gives two copies of the same term, which still can't produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates 11-30:** These contain `x*log(c*|v| + 1)`. The function `log(c*|v|+1)` is NOT equivalent to `|v|^(1/3)` for any constant. These are fundamentally different basis functions (logarithmic vs power law). So these cannot match.

**Candidates with `tanh` terms:** `tanh(c*x)` is not equivalent to any term in GT. Setting `c0=0` eliminates it, but the remaining terms still need to match.

Let me specifically check candidates with `v**c*x` AND `v**c*x` where one could potentially handle the sign issue... No, `v^(1/3)` for negative `v` gives a negative value (real cube root), while `|v|^(1/3)` gives positive. These are fundamentally different.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can exactly reproduce the `x*|v|^(1/3)` term. The candidates either use `v^c*x` (which differs from `|v|^c*x` for negative `v`) or `x*log(c*|v|+1)` (wrong basis function).
